Biodiversity is also important to the security of resources such as water, timber, paper, fiber and food.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> As a result, biodiversity loss is a significant risk factor in business development and a threat to long term economic sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure.2C_cultural_and_aesthetic_value">Leisure, cultural and aesthetic value</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Leisure, cultural and aesthetic value">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biodiversity enriches leisure activities such as <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">birdwatching</a> or natural history study. Biodiversity inspires <a href="/wiki/Musician" title="Musician">musicians</a>, painters, sculptors, writers and other artists. Many cultures view themselves as an integral part of the natural world which requires them to respect other living organisms.</p>
<p>Popular activities such as <a href="/wiki/Gardening" title="Gardening">gardening</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishkeeping" title="Fishkeeping">fishkeeping</a> and specimen collecting strongly depend on biodiversity. The number of species involved in such pursuits is in the tens of thousands, though the majority do not enter commerce.</p>
<p>The relationships between the original natural areas of these often exotic animals and plants and commercial collectors, suppliers, breeders, propagators and those who promote their understanding and enjoyment are complex and poorly understood. The general public responds well to exposure to rare and unusual organisms, reflecting their inherent value.</p>
<p>Philosophically it could be argued that biodiversity has intrinsic aesthetic and spiritual value to <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">mankind</a> <i>in and of itself</i>. This idea can be used as a counterweight to the notion that <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical forest">tropical forests</a> and other ecological realms are only worthy of conservation because of the services they provide.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_services">Ecological services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ecological services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ecological_effects_of_biodiversity" title="Ecological effects of biodiversity">Ecological effects of biodiversity</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg/170px-Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg/255px-Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg/340px-Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eaglecreek-28July2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eagle_Creek_(Multnomah_County,_Oregon)" title="Eagle Creek (Multnomah County, Oregon)">Eagle Creek</a>, Oregon hiking</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Biodiversity supports many <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a>:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"There is now unequivocal evidence that biodiversity loss reduces the efficiency by which ecological communities capture biologically essential resources, produce biomass, decompose and recycle biologically essential nutrients... There is mounting evidence that biodiversity increases the stability of ecosystem functions through time... Diverse communities are more productive because they contain key species that have a large influence on productivity and differences in functional traits among organisms increase total resource capture... The impacts of diversity loss on ecological processes might be sufficiently large to rival the impacts of many other global drivers of environmental change... Maintaining multiple ecosystem processes at multiple places and times requires higher levels of biodiversity than does a single process at a single place and time."<sup id="cite_ref-diversity-loss-and-its-impact_80-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-loss-and-its-impact-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>It plays a part in regulating the chemistry of our <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">atmosphere</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a>. Biodiversity is directly involved in <a href="/wiki/Water_purification" title="Water purification">water purification</a>, recycling <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a> and providing fertile soils. Experiments with controlled environments have shown that humans cannot easily build ecosystems to support human needs;<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> for example <a href="/wiki/Entomophily" title="Entomophily">insect pollination</a> cannot be mimicked,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and that activity alone represented between $2.1-14.6 billions in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Number_of_species">Number of species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Number of species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Global_biodiversity" title="Global biodiversity">Global biodiversity</a></div>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png/700px-Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png" width="700" height="334" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png/1050px-Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png/1400px-Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png 2x" data-file-width="4103" data-file-height="1958" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mora_2011_Predicted_and_Unpredicted_species.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Discovered and predicted total number of species on land and in the oceans</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to Mora and colleagues, the total number of terrestrial species is estimated to be around 8.7 million while the number of oceanic species is much lower, estimated at 2.2 million. The authors note that these estimates are strongest for eukaryotic organisms and likely represent the lower bound of prokaryote diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-mora2011_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mora2011-130">[130]</a></sup> Other estimates include:</p>
<ul>
<li>220,000 <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Vascular plants">vascular plants</a>, estimated using the species-area relation method<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>0.7-1 million marine species<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li>10–30 million <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insects</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> (of some 0.9 million we know today)<sup id="cite_ref-Le_Monde_newspaper_article_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Le_Monde_newspaper_article-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li>5–10 million <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li>1.5-3 million <a href="/wiki/Fungi" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungi">fungi</a>, estimates based on data from the tropics, long-term non-tropical sites and molecular studies that have revealed <a href="/wiki/Cryptic_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Cryptic species">cryptic speciation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Some 0.075 million species of fungi had been documented by 2001)<sup id="cite_ref-Hawksworth_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hawksworth-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li>1 million <a href="/wiki/Mite" title="Mite">mites</a><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li>The number of <a href="/wiki/Microbial" class="mw-redirect" title="Microbial">microbial</a> species is not reliably known, but the <a href="/wiki/Global_Ocean_Sampling_Expedition" title="Global Ocean Sampling Expedition">Global Ocean Sampling Expedition</a> dramatically increased the estimates of genetic diversity by identifying an enormous number of new genes from near-surface <a href="/wiki/Plankton" title="Plankton">plankton</a> samples at various marine locations, initially over the 2004-2006 period.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The findings may eventually cause a significant change in the way science defines <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> and other taxonomic categories.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Since the rate of extinction has increased, many extant species may become extinct before they are described.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Not surprisingly, in the <a href="/wiki/Animalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Animalia">animalia</a> the most studied groups are <a href="/wiki/Birds" class="mw-redirect" title="Birds">birds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mammals" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammals">mammals</a>, whereas <a href="/wiki/Fishes" class="mw-redirect" title="Fishes">fishes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthropods" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthropods">arthropods</a> are the least studied <a href="/wiki/Animals" class="mw-redirect" title="Animals">animals</a> groups.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measuring_biodiversity">Measuring biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Measuring biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Diversity_index" title="Diversity index">diversity index</a> and <a href="/wiki/Measurement_of_biodiversity" title="Measurement of biodiversity">measurement of biodiversity</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Species_loss_rates">Species loss rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Species loss rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Loss_of_biodiversity" class="mw-redirect" title="Loss of biodiversity">loss of biodiversity</a></div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>No longer do we have to justify the existence of humid tropical forests on the feeble grounds that they might carry plants with drugs that cure human disease. <a href="/wiki/Gaia_hypothesis" title="Gaia hypothesis"><i>Gaia theory</i></a> forces us to see that they offer much more than this. Through their capacity to evapotranspirate vast volumes of water vapor, they serve to keep the planet cool by wearing a sunshade of white reflecting cloud. Their replacement by cropland could precipitate a disaster that is global in scale.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>During the last century, decreases in biodiversity have been increasingly observed. In 2007, German Federal Environment Minister <a href="/wiki/Sigmar_Gabriel" title="Sigmar Gabriel">Sigmar Gabriel</a> cited estimates that up to 30% of all species will be extinct by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Of these, about one eighth of known plant species are threatened with <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity-145">[145]</a></sup> Estimates reach as high as 140,000 species per year (based on <a href="/wiki/Species-area_curve" class="mw-redirect" title="Species-area curve">Species-area theory</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> This figure indicates <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">unsustainable</a> ecological practices, because few species emerge each year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Almost all scientists acknowledge that the rate of species loss is greater now than at any time in human history, with extinctions occurring at rates hundreds of times higher than <a href="/wiki/Background_extinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Background extinction">background extinction</a> rates.<sup id="cite_ref-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reid_Reversing_loss_of_Biodiversity-145">[145]</a></sup> As of 2012, some studies suggest that 25% of all mammal species could be extinct in 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>In absolute terms, the planet has lost 52% of its biodiversity since 1970 according to a 2014 study by the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>. The Living Planet Report 2014 claims that "the number of mammals, birds, reptiles, amphibians and fish across the globe is, on average, about half the size it was 40 years ago". Of that number, 39% accounts for the terrestrial wildlife gone, 39% for the marine wildlife gone and 76% for the freshwater wildlife gone. Biodiversity took the biggest hit in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, plummeting 83 percent. High-income countries showed a 10% increase in biodiversity, which was canceled out by a loss in low-income countries. This is despite the fact that high-income countries use five times the ecological resources of low-income countries, which was explained as a result of process whereby wealthy nations are outsourcing resource depletion to poorer nations, which are suffering the greatest ecosystem losses.<sup id="cite_ref-LivingPlanetReport2014_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LivingPlanetReport2014-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Threats">Threats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Threats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2006 many species were formally classified as <a href="/wiki/Rare_species" title="Rare species">rare</a> or <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a> or <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">threatened</a>; moreover, scientists have estimated that millions more species are at risk which have not been formally recognized. About 40 percent of the 40,177 species assessed using the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> criteria are now listed as threatened with <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a>—a total of 16,119.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jared_Diamond" title="Jared Diamond">Jared Diamond</a> describes an "Evil Quartet" of habitat destruction, overkill, introduced species and secondary extinctions.<sup id="cite_ref-MoultonSanderson1998_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoultonSanderson1998-150">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_O._Wilson" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward O. Wilson">Edward O. Wilson</a> prefers the <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronym</a> HIPPO, standing for <b>H</b>abitat destruction, <b>I</b>nvasive species, <b>P</b>ollution, human over-<b>P</b>opulation and <b>O</b>ver-harvesting.<sup id="cite_ref-Chen2003_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chen2003-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The most authoritative classification in use today is <a href="/wiki/IUCN" class="mw-redirect" title="IUCN">IUCN</a>'s Classification of Direct Threats<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> which has been adopted by major international conservation organizations such as the US <a href="/wiki/Nature_Conservancy" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature Conservancy">Nature Conservancy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a> and <a href="/wiki/BirdLife_International" title="BirdLife International">BirdLife International</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Habitat_destruction">Habitat destruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Habitat destruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazonie_deforestation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Amazonie_deforestation.jpg/220px-Amazonie_deforestation.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Amazonie_deforestation.jpg/330px-Amazonie_deforestation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Amazonie_deforestation.jpg/440px-Amazonie_deforestation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="778" data-file-height="618" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazonie_deforestation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">Deforestation</a> and increased road-building in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a> are a significant concern because of increased human encroachment upon wild areas, increased resource extraction and further threats to biodiversity.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">Habitat destruction</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitat (ecology)">Habitat</a> destruction has played a key role in extinctions, especially related to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical forest">tropical forest</a> destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-EhrlichEhrlich1983_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EhrlichEhrlich1983-154">[154]</a></sup> Factors contributing to habitat loss are: <a href="/wiki/Overconsumption" title="Overconsumption">overconsumption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">overpopulation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Land_use,_land-use_change_and_forestry" title="Land use, land-use change and forestry">land use change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> (<a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soil_contamination" title="Soil contamination">soil contamination</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> or climate change.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Habitat size and numbers of species are systematically related. Physically larger species and those living at lower latitudes or in forests or oceans are more sensitive to reduction in habitat area.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Conversion to "trivial" standardized ecosystems (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Monoculture" title="Monoculture">monoculture</a> following <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>) effectively destroys habitat for the more diverse species that preceded the conversion. In some countries lack of property rights or lax law/regulatory enforcement necessarily leads to biodiversity loss (degradation costs having to be supported by the community).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A 2007 study conducted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> found that biodiversity and genetic diversity are codependent—that diversity among species requires diversity within a species and vice versa. "If any one type is removed from the system, the cycle can break down and the community becomes dominated by a single species."<sup id="cite_ref-enn_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enn-157">[157]</a></sup> At present, the most threatened ecosystems are found in <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Ecosystem_Assessment" title="Millennium Ecosystem Assessment">Millennium Ecosystem Assessment</a> 2005, which was confirmed by the "Freshwater Animal Diversity Assessment", organised by the <a href="/wiki/GBIF" class="mw-redirect" title="GBIF">biodiversity platform</a> and the French <i><a href="/wiki/Institut_de_recherche_pour_le_d%C3%A9veloppement" title="Institut de recherche pour le développement">Institut de recherche pour le développement</a></i> (MNHNP).<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>Co-extinctions are a form of habitat destruction. Co-extinction occurs when the extinction or decline in one accompanies the other, such as in plants and beetles.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Introduced_and_invasive_species">Introduced and invasive species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Introduced and invasive species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">Introduced species</a> and <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">Invasive species</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg/220px-Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg/330px-Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2b/Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Male_Silver_Pheasant.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Male <i>Lophura nycthemera</i> (<a href="/wiki/Silver_pheasant" title="Silver pheasant">silver pheasant</a>), a native of <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> that has been introduced into parts of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> for ornamental reasons</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Barriers such as large <a href="/wiki/Rivers" class="mw-redirect" title="Rivers">rivers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">seas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceans" class="mw-redirect" title="Oceans">oceans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountains">mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deserts" class="mw-redirect" title="Deserts">deserts</a> encourage diversity by enabling independent evolution on either side of the barrier, via the process of <a href="/wiki/Allopatric_speciation" title="Allopatric speciation">allopatric speciation</a>. The term <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a> is applied to species that breach the natural barriers that would normally keep them constrained. Without barriers, such species occupy new territory, often supplanting native species by occupying their niches, or by using resources that would normally sustain native species.</p>
<p>The number of species invasions has been on the rise at least since the beginning of the 1900s. Species are increasingly being moved by humans (on purpose and accidentally). In some cases the invaders are causing drastic changes and damage to their new habitats (e.g.: zebra mussels and the emerald ash borer in the Great Lakes region and the lion fish along the North American Atlantic coast). Some evidence suggests that invasive species are competitive in their new habitats because they are subject to less pathogen disturbance.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Others report confounding evidence that occasionally suggest that species-rich communities harbor many native and exotic species simultaneously<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> while some say that diverse ecosystems are more resilient and resist invasive plants and animals.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> An important question is, "do invasive species cause extinctions?" Many studies cite effects of invasive species on natives,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> but not extinctions. Invasive species seem to increase local (i.e.: <a href="/wiki/Alpha_diversity" title="Alpha diversity">alpha diversity</a>) diversity, which decreases turnover of diversity (i.e.: <a href="/wiki/Beta_diversity" title="Beta diversity">beta diversity</a>). Overall <a href="/wiki/Gamma_diversity" title="Gamma diversity">gamma diversity</a> may be lowered because species are going extinct because of other causes,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> but even some of the most insidious invaders (e.g.: Dutch elm disease, emerald ash borer, chestnut blight in North America) have not caused their host species to become extinct. <a href="/wiki/Local_extinction" title="Local extinction">Extirpation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_decline" title="Population decline">population decline</a> and <a href="/wiki/Species_homogeneity" title="Species homogeneity">homogenization</a> of regional biodiversity are much more common. Human activities have frequently been the cause of invasive species circumventing their barriers,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> by introducing them for food and other purposes. Human activities therefore allow species to migrate to new areas (and thus become invasive) occurred on time scales much shorter than historically have been required for a species to extend its range.</p>
<p>Not all introduced species are invasive, nor all invasive species deliberately introduced. In cases such as the <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">zebra mussel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasion</a> of US waterways was unintentional. In other cases, such as <a href="/wiki/Mongoose" title="Mongoose">mongooses</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, the introduction is deliberate but ineffective (<a href="/wiki/Nocturnal" class="mw-redirect" title="Nocturnal">nocturnal</a> <a href="/wiki/Rat" title="Rat">rats</a> were not vulnerable to the <a href="/wiki/Diurnality" title="Diurnality">diurnal</a> mongoose). In other cases, such as <a href="/wiki/Oil_palm" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil palm">oil palms</a> in Indonesia and Malaysia, the introduction produces substantial economic benefits, but the benefits are accompanied by costly <a href="/wiki/Unintended_consequences" title="Unintended consequences">unintended consequences</a>.</p>
<p>Finally, an introduced species may unintentionally injure a species that depends on the species it replaces. In <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prunus_spinosa" title="Prunus spinosa">Prunus spinosa</a> from Eastern Europe leafs much sooner than its West European counterparts, disrupting the feeding habits of the <i><a href="/wiki/Thecla_betulae" class="mw-redirect" title="Thecla betulae">Thecla betulae</a></i> butterfly (which feeds on the leaves). Introducing new species often leaves endemic and other local species unable to compete with the exotic species and unable to survive. The exotic organisms may be <a href="/wiki/Predator" class="mw-redirect" title="Predator">predators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parasite" class="mw-redirect" title="Parasite">parasites</a>, or may simply outcompete indigenous species for nutrients, water and light.</p>
<p>At present, several countries have already imported so many exotic species, particularly agricultural and ornamental plants, that their own indigenous fauna/flora may be outnumbered. For example, the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Kudzu" title="Kudzu">kudzu</a> from Southeast Asia to Canada and the United States has threatened biodiversity in certain areas.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetic_pollution">Genetic pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Genetic pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Genetic_pollution" title="Genetic pollution">Genetic pollution</a></div>
<p>Endemic species can be threatened with <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> through the process of <a href="/wiki/Genetic_pollution" title="Genetic pollution">genetic pollution</a>, i.e. uncontrolled <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybridization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Introgression" title="Introgression">introgression</a> and genetic swamping. Genetic pollution leads to homogenization or replacement of local <a href="/wiki/Genomes" class="mw-redirect" title="Genomes">genomes</a> as a result of either a numerical and/or <a href="/wiki/Fitness_(biology)" title="Fitness (biology)">fitness</a> advantage of an introduced species.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Hybridization and introgression are side-effects of introduction and invasion. These phenomena can be especially detrimental to <a href="/wiki/Rare_species" title="Rare species">rare species</a> that come into contact with more abundant ones. The abundant species can interbreed with the rare species, swamping its <a href="/wiki/Gene_pool" title="Gene pool">gene pool</a>. This problem is not always apparent from <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphological</a> (outward appearance) observations alone. Some degree of <a href="/wiki/Gene_flow" title="Gene flow">gene flow</a> is normal adaptation and not all <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">gene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genotype" title="Genotype">genotype</a> constellations can be preserved. However, hybridization with or without introgression may, nevertheless, threaten a rare species' existence.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PottsBarbour2001_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PottsBarbour2001-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overexploitation">Overexploitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Overexploitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">Overexploitation</a></div>
<p>Overexploitation occurs when a resource is consumed at an unsustainable rate. This occurs on land in the form of <a href="/wiki/Overhunting" class="mw-redirect" title="Overhunting">overhunting</a>, excessive <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">logging</a>, poor <a href="/wiki/Soil_conservation" title="Soil conservation">soil conservation</a> in agriculture and the illegal <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_trade" title="Wildlife trade">wildlife trade</a>.</p>
<p>About 25% of world <a href="/wiki/Fishery" title="Fishery">fisheries</a> are now overfished to the point where their current biomass is less than the level that maximizes their sustainable yield.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Overkill_hypothesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Overkill hypothesis">overkill hypothesis</a>, a pattern of large animal extinctions connected with <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">human migration</a> patterns, can be used explain why <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">megafaunal</a> extinctions can occur within a relatively short time period.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hybridization.2C_genetic_pollution.2Ferosion_and_food_security">Hybridization, genetic pollution/erosion and food security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Hybridization, genetic pollution/erosion and food security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg/220px-Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="252" data-file-height="189" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wheat_selection_k10183-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Yecoro <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> (right) <a href="/wiki/Cultivar" title="Cultivar">cultivar</a> is sensitive to salinity, plants resulting from a hybrid cross with cultivar W4910 (left) show greater tolerance to high salinity</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">Food security</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genetic_erosion" title="Genetic erosion">Genetic erosion</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a> popularized the use of conventional <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">hybridization</a> to increase yield. Often hybridized breeds originated in developed countries and were further hybridized with local varieties in the developing world to create high yield strains resistant to local climate and diseases. Local governments and industry have been pushing hybridization. Formerly huge gene pools of various wild and indigenous breeds have collapsed causing widespread <a href="/wiki/Genetic_erosion" title="Genetic erosion">genetic erosion</a> and genetic pollution. This has resulted in loss of genetic diversity and biodiversity as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-bulletin28_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bulletin28-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organism" title="Genetically modified organism">Genetically modified organisms</a> contain genetic material that is altered through <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetic engineering</a>. Genetically modified <a href="/wiki/Crop" title="Crop">crops</a> have become a common source for genetic pollution in not only wild varieties, but also in domesticated varieties derived from classical hybridization.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zaid1999_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaid1999-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>Genetic erosion and genetic pollution have the potential to destroy unique <a href="/wiki/Genotype" title="Genotype">genotypes</a>, threatening future access to <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>. A decrease in genetic diversity weakens the ability of crops and livestock to be hybridized to resist disease and survive changes in climate.<sup id="cite_ref-bulletin28_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bulletin28-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_climate_change_on_plant_biodiversity" class="mw-redirect" title="Effect of climate change on plant biodiversity">Effect of climate change on plant biodiversity</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/220px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/330px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/440px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1575" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">Polar bears</a> on the sea ice of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>. Climate change has started affecting bear populations.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Global warming is also considered to be a major potential threat to global biodiversity in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kannan2009_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kannan2009-180">[180]</a></sup> For example, coral reefs - which are biodiversity hotspots - will be lost within the century if global warming continues at the current trend.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>Climate change has seen many claims about potential to affect biodiversity but evidence supporting the statement is tenuous. Increasing atmospheric carbon dioxide certainly affects plant morphology<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> and is acidifying oceans,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> and temperature affects species ranges,<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LovejoyHannah2005_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LovejoyHannah2005-187">[187]</a></sup> phenology,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> and weather,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> but the major impacts that have been predicted are still just <i>potential</i> impacts. We have not documented major extinctions yet, even as climate change drastically alters the biology of many species.</p>
<p>In 2004, an international collaborative study on four continents estimated that 10 percent of species would become extinct by 2050 because of global warming. "We need to limit climate change or we wind up with a lot of species in trouble, possibly extinct," said Dr. Lee Hannah, a co-author of the paper and chief climate change biologist at the Center for Applied Biodiversity Science at Conservation International.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>A recent study predicts that up to 35% of the world terrestrial carnivores and ungulates will be at higher risk of extinction by 2050 because of the joint effects of predicted climate and land-use change under business-as-usual human development scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_overpopulation">Human overpopulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Human overpopulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">Human overpopulation</a></div>
<p>From 1950 to 2011, world population increased from 2.5 billion to 7 billion and is forecast to reach a plateau of more than 9 billion during the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Some recent forecasts place the possible number of people on the planet at 11 billion or 15 billion by 2100.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Sir <a href="/wiki/David_King_(scientist)" class="mw-redirect" title="David King (scientist)">David King</a>, former chief scientific adviser to the UK government, told a parliamentary inquiry: <i>"It is self-evident that the massive growth in the <a href="/wiki/Human_population" class="mw-redirect" title="Human population">human population</a> through the 20th century has had more impact on biodiversity than any other single factor."</i><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> At least until the middle of the 21st century, worldwide losses of pristine biodiverse land will probably depend much on the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">human birth rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> Biologists such as <a href="/wiki/Paul_R._Ehrlich" title="Paul R. Ehrlich">Paul R. Ehrlich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Pimm" title="Stuart Pimm">Stuart Pimm</a> have noted that <a href="/wiki/Human_population_growth" class="mw-redirect" title="Human population growth">human population growth</a> is one of the main drivers of species extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to a 2014 study by the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a>, the global human population already exceeds planet's <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> - it would take the equivalent of 1.5 Earths of biocapacity to meet our current demands.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The report further points that if everyone on the planet had the Footprint of the average resident of Qatar, we would need 4.8 Earths and if we lived the lifestyle of a typical resident of the USA, we would need 3.9 Earths.<sup id="cite_ref-LivingPlanetReport2014_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LivingPlanetReport2014-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Holocene_extinction">The Holocene extinction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: The Holocene extinction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction">Holocene extinction</a></div>
<p>Rates of decline in biodiversity in this sixth mass extinction match or exceed rates of loss in the five previous <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">mass extinction events</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Fossil_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil record">fossil record</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-proceedings1_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proceedings1-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Loss of biodiversity results in the loss of <a href="/wiki/Natural_capital" title="Natural capital">natural capital</a> that supplies <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem goods and services</a>. From the perspective of the method known as Natural Economy the economic value of 17 ecosystem services for Earth's <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a> (calculated in 1997) has an estimated value of US$33 trillion (3.3x10<sup>13</sup>) per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Costanza97_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costanza97-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation">Conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">Conservation biology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/220px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/330px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/440px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1398" data-file-height="1398" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A schematic image illustrating the relationship between biodiversity, ecosystem services, human well-being and poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> The illustration shows where conservation action, strategies and plans can influence the drivers of the current biodiversity crisis at local, regional, to global scales.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gletscherschmelze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/300px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg" width="300" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/450px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/600px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="519" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gletscherschmelze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">retreat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aletsch_Glacier" title="Aletsch Glacier">Aletsch Glacier</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Alps" title="Swiss Alps">Swiss Alps</a> (situation in 1979, 1991 and 2002), due to <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">Conservation biology</a> matured in the mid-20th century as <a href="/wiki/Ecologists" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecologists">ecologists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naturalists" class="mw-redirect" title="Naturalists">naturalists</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Scientists" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientists">scientists</a> began to research and address issues pertaining to global biodiversity declines.<sup id="cite_ref-Soule86_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Davis96_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davis96-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dyke2008_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dyke2008-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>The conservation ethic advocates management of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> for the purpose of sustaining biodiversity in <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecosystems">ecosystems</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolutionary process</a> and human culture and society.<sup id="cite_ref-proceedings1_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proceedings1-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Soule86_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dyke2008_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dyke2008-214">[214]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hunter1996_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hunter1996-215">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<p>Conservation biology is reforming around strategic plans to protect biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Soule86_212-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Soul.C3.A91986_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soul.C3.A91986-217">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> Preserving global biodiversity is a priority in strategic conservation plans that are designed to engage public policy and concerns affecting local, regional and global scales of communities, ecosystems and cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Action plans identify <a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics#Methodology" title="Ecological economics">ways</a> of sustaining human well-being, employing <a href="/wiki/Natural_capital" title="Natural capital">natural capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">market capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/w/index.php?title=EU_Directive_1999/22/EC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EU Directive 1999/22/EC (page does not exist)">EU Directive 1999/22/EC</a> zoos are described as having a role in the preservation of the biodiversity of wildlife animals by conducting research or participation in <a href="/wiki/Breeding_program" title="Breeding program">breeding programs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protection_and_restoration_techniques">Protection and restoration techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Protection and restoration techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Removal of exotic species will allow the species that they have negatively impacted to recover their ecological niches. Exotic species that have become pests can be identified taxonomically (e.g.,&#160;with <a href="/wiki/Digital_Automated_Identification_SYstem" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital Automated Identification SYstem">Digital Automated Identification SYstem</a> (DAISY), using the <a href="/wiki/Consortium_for_the_Barcode_of_Life" title="Consortium for the Barcode of Life">barcode of life</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Removal is practical only given large groups of individuals due to the economic cost.</p>
<p>As sustainable populations of the remaining native species in an area become assured, "missing" species that are candidates for reintroduction can be identified using databases such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_of_Life#Resources_and_collaborations" title="Encyclopedia of Life">Encyclopedia of Life</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_Biodiversity_Information_Facility" title="Global Biodiversity Information Facility">Global Biodiversity Information Facility</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_banking" title="Biodiversity banking">Biodiversity banking</a> places a monetary value on biodiversity. One example is the Australian <a href="/wiki/Native_Vegetation_Management_Framework" title="Native Vegetation Management Framework">Native Vegetation Management Framework</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gene_bank" title="Gene bank">Gene banks</a> are collections of specimens and genetic material. Some banks intend to reintroduce banked species to the ecosystem (e.g.,&#160;via tree nurseries).<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></li>
<li>Reduction of and better targeting of pesticides allows more species to survive in agricultural and urbanized areas.</li>
<li>Location-specific approaches may be less useful for protecting migratory species. One approach is to create <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_corridor" title="Wildlife corridor">wildlife corridors</a> that correspond to the animals' movements. National and other boundaries can complicate corridor creation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protected_areas">Protected areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Protected areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(April 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Protected areas is meant for affording protection to wild animals and their habitat which also includes forest reserves and biosphere reserves. Protected areas have been set up all over the world with the specific aim of protecting and conserving plants and animals.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_parks">National parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: National parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">National park</a></div>
<p>National park and nature reserve is the area selected by governments or private organizations for special protection against damage or degradation with the objective of biodiversity and landscape conservation. National parks are usually owned and managed by national or state governments. A limit is placed on the number of visitors permitted to enter certain fragile areas. Designated trails or roads are created. The visitors are allowed to enter only for study, cultural and recreation purposes. Forestry operations, grazing of animals and hunting of animals are regulated. Exploitation of habitat or wildlife is banned.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_sanctuary">Wildlife sanctuary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Wildlife sanctuary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Wildlife sanctuary aims only at conservation of species and have the following features:</p>
<ol>
<li>The boundaries of the sanctuaries are not limited by state legislation.</li>
<li>The killing, hunting or capturing of any species is prohibited except by or under the control of the highest authority in the department which is responsible for the management of the sanctuary.</li>
<li>Private ownership may be allowed.</li>
<li>Forestry and other usages can also be permitted.</li>
</ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forest_reserves">Forest reserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Forest reserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The forests play a vital role in harbouring more than 45,000 floral and 81,000 faunal species of which 5150 floral and 1837 faunal species are endemic. Plant and animal species confined to a specific geographical area are called endemic species. In reserved forests, rights to activities like hunting and grazing are sometimes given to communities living on the fringes of the forest, who sustain their livelihood partially or wholly from forest resources or products. The unclassed forests covers 6.4 percent of the total forest area and they are marked by the following characteristics:</p>
<ol>
<li>They are large inaccessible forests.</li>
<li>Many of these are unoccupied.</li>
<li>They are ecologically and economically less important.</li>
</ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Steps_to_conserve_the_forest_cover">Steps to conserve the forest cover</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Steps to conserve the forest cover">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ol>
<li>An extensive reforestation/afforestation program should be followed.</li>
<li>Alternative environment-friendly sources of fuel energy such as biogas other than wood should be used.</li>
<li>Loss of biodiversity due to forest fire is a major problem, immediate steps to prevent forest fire need to be taken.</li>
<li>Overgrazing by cattle can damage a forest seriously. Therefore, certain steps should be taken to prevent overgrazing by cattle.</li>
<li>Hunting and poaching should be banned.</li>
</ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoological_parks">Zoological parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Zoological parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In zoological parks or zoos, live animals are kept for public recreation, education and conservation purposes. Modern zoos offer veterinary facilities, provide opportunities for threatened species to breed in captivity and usually build environments that simulate the native habitats of the animals in their care. Zoos play a major role in creating awareness among common people about the need to conserve nature.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Botanical_gardens">Botanical gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Botanical gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Botanical garden is a garden in which plants are grown and displayed primarily for scientific and educational purposes. It consists of a collection of living plants, grown outdoors or under glass in greenhouses and conservatories. In addition, it includes a collection of dried plants or herbarium and such facilities as lecture rooms, laboratories, libraries, museums and experimental or research plantings.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Resource_allocation">Resource allocation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Resource allocation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Focusing on limited areas of higher potential biodiversity promises greater immediate return on investment than spreading resources evenly or focusing on areas of little diversity but greater interest in biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup></p>
<p>A second strategy focuses on areas that retain most of their original diversity, which typically require little or no restoration. These are typically non-urbanized, non-agricultural areas. Tropical areas often fit both criteria, given their natively high diversity and relative lack of development.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">Legal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Legal status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hopetoun_falls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/220px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/330px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/440px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hopetoun_falls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A great deal of work is occurring to preserve the natural characteristics of <a href="/wiki/Hopetoun_Falls" title="Hopetoun Falls">Hopetoun Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> while continuing to allow visitor access.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>United Nations <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> (1992) and <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_Protocol_on_Biosafety" title="Cartagena Protocol on Biosafety">Cartagena Protocol on Biosafety</a>;</li>
<li>Convention on International Trade in Endangered Species (<a href="/wiki/CITES" title="CITES">CITES</a>);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ramsar_Convention" title="Ramsar Convention">Ramsar Convention</a> (Wetlands);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bonn_Convention" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonn Convention">Bonn Convention</a> on Migratory Species;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Convention" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Convention">World Heritage Convention</a> (indirectly by protecting biodiversity habitats)</li>
<li>Regional Conventions such as the Apia Convention</li>
<li>Bilateral agreements such as the <a href="/wiki/Japan-Australia_Migratory_Bird_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Japan-Australia Migratory Bird Agreement">Japan-Australia Migratory Bird Agreement</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Global agreements such as the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a>, give "sovereign national rights over biological resources" (not property). The agreements commit countries to "conserve biodiversity", "develop resources for sustainability" and "share the benefits" resulting from their use. Biodiverse countries that allow <a href="/wiki/Bioprospecting" title="Bioprospecting">bioprospecting</a> or collection of natural products, expect a share of the benefits rather than allowing the individual or institution that discovers/exploits the resource to capture them privately. Bioprospecting can become a type of <a href="/wiki/Biopiracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Biopiracy">biopiracy</a> when such principles are not respected.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Sovereignty principles can rely upon what is better known as <a href="/wiki/International_Treaty_on_Plant_Genetic_Resources_for_Food_and_Agriculture" title="International Treaty on Plant Genetic Resources for Food and Agriculture">Access and Benefit Sharing Agreements</a> (ABAs). The Convention on Biodiversity implies <a href="/wiki/Informed_consent" title="Informed consent">informed consent</a> between the source country and the collector, to establish which resource will be used and for what and to settle on a <a href="/wiki/International_Treaty_on_Plant_Genetic_Resources_for_Food_and_Agriculture" title="International Treaty on Plant Genetic Resources for Food and Agriculture">fair agreement on benefit sharing</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_level_laws">National level laws</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: National level laws">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biodiversity is taken into account in some political and judicial decisions:</p>
<ul>
<li>The relationship between law and ecosystems is very ancient and has consequences for biodiversity. It is related to private and public property rights. It can define protection for threatened ecosystems, but also some rights and duties (for example, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and hunting rights).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Law regarding species is more recent. It defines species that must be protected because they may be threatened by extinction. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Endangered_Species_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Endangered Species Act">Endangered Species Act</a> is an example of an attempt to address the "law and species" issue.</li>
<li>Laws regarding gene pools are only about a century old.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Domestication and plant breeding methods are not new, but advances in genetic engineering have led to tighter laws covering distribution of <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Genetically modified organisms">genetically modified organisms</a>, gene <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a> and process patents.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Governments struggle to decide whether to focus on for example, genes, genomes, or organisms and species.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Uniform approval for use of biodiversity as a legal standard has not been achieved, however. Bosselman argues that biodiversity should not be used as a legal standard, claiming that the remaining areas of scientific uncertainty cause unacceptable administrative waste and increase litigation without promoting preservation goals.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup></p>
<p>India passed the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Biological_Diversity_Act&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Biological Diversity Act (page does not exist)">Biological Diversity Act</a> in 2002 for the conservation of biological diversity in India. The Act also provides mechanisms for equitable sharing of benefits from the use of traditional biological resources and knowledge.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analytical_limits">Analytical limits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Analytical limits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomic_and_size_relationships">Taxonomic and size relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Taxonomic and size relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Less than 1% of all species that have been described have been studied beyond simply noting their existence.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> The vast majority of Earth's species are microbial. Contemporary biodiversity physics is "firmly fixated on the visible [macroscopic] world".<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> For example, microbial life is <a href="/wiki/Metabolically" class="mw-redirect" title="Metabolically">metabolically</a> and environmentally more diverse than multicellular life (see e.g., <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophile</a>). "On the tree of life, based on analyses of small-subunit <a href="/wiki/Ribosomal_RNA" title="Ribosomal RNA">ribosomal RNA</a>, visible life consists of barely noticeable twigs. The inverse relationship of size and population recurs higher on the evolutionary ladder—"to a first approximation, all multicellular species on Earth are insects".<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> Insect extinction rates are high—supporting the Holocene extinction hypothesis. <sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://natureserve.org/">NatureServe: This site serves as a portal for accessing several types of publicly available biodiversity data</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://css.snre.umich.edu/css_doc/CSS09-08.pdf">Biodiversity Factsheet</a> by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>'s Center for Sustainable Systems</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://savingspecies.org/2012/stunning-new-biodiversity-maps-show-where-to-prioritize-conservation/">Color-coded images of vertebrate biodiversity hotspots</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.paf.net.pk/">Pakistan Avicultural Foundation</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Documents">Documents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Documents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.millenniumassessment.org/documents/document.354.aspx.pdf">Biodiversity Synthesis Report</a> (PDF) by the Millennium Ecosystem Assessment (MA, 2005)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biodiversityhotspots.org/xp/hotspots/Documents/cihotspotmap.pdf">Conservation International hotspot map</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://pdf.usaid.gov/pdf_docs/pbaae019.pdf">Zhuravlev, Yu. N., ed. (2000) <i>Стратегия сохранения биоразнообразия Сихотэ-Алиня = A Biodiversity Conservation Strategy for the Sikhote-Alin'</i> Vladivostok: Russian Academy of Sciences, Far Eastern Branch</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tools">Tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.globio.info/">GLOBIO</a>, an ongoing programme to map the past, current and future impacts of human activities on biodiversity</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://stort.unep-wcmc.org/imaps/gb2002/book/viewer.htm">World Map of Biodiversity</a> an interactive map from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Conservation_Monitoring_Centre" title="World Conservation Monitoring Centre">World Conservation Monitoring Centre</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bison.usgs.gov/#home">Biodiversity Information Serving Our Nation (BISON)</a>, provides a United States gateway for serving, searching, mapping and downloading integrated species occurrence records from multiple data sources</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resources">Resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/">Biodiversity Heritage Library</a> – Open access digital library of taxonomic literature</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biodiversitymapping.org/">Mapping of biodiversity</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eol.org/">Encyclopedia of Life</a> – Documenting all species of life on earth</li>
</ul>
